Another example¶

In this notebook, we'll try to predict the price of a house which follows a simple pricing rule. In reality, the cost of a house depends on a lot of factors, but let's just keep it simple for the time being. We begin by importing some standard packages.

In [1]:
import tensorflow as tf
import numpy as np
from tensorflow import keras

House price¶

Let's consider a simple pricing scheme.

Cost = 50k + (number_of_bedrooms * 50k)

Thus, cost of a one bedroom house is 100k, cost of a two bedroom house is 150k and so on. Let's generate some data that satisfies this rule.

In [2]:
X = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]
y = [50000 + x*50000 for x in X]

for t in list(zip(X,y)):
    print('#bedrooms: {} | cost of house: ${}'.format(t[0], t[1]))

#bedrooms: 1 | cost of house: $100000
#bedrooms: 2 | cost of house: $150000
#bedrooms: 3 | cost of house: $200000
#bedrooms: 4 | cost of house: $250000
#bedrooms: 5 | cost of house: $300000
#bedrooms: 6 | cost of house: $350000

Create a neural network model¶

Again, let's go with the same model which I used in the previous notebook. i.e. a single neuron with 1 input and 1 output.

In [3]:
model = keras.Sequential([keras.layers.Dense(units=1, input_shape=[1])])

WARNING:tensorflow:From /home/tanmay/anaconda3/lib/python3.7/site-packages/tensorflow/python/ops/resource_variable_ops.py:435: colocate_with (from tensorflow.python.framework.ops) is deprecated and will be removed in a future version.
Instructions for updating:
Colocations handled automatically by placer.

Compile the model¶

In [4]:
model.compile(loss='mean_squared_error', optimizer='sgd')

WARNING:tensorflow:From /home/tanmay/anaconda3/lib/python3.7/site-packages/tensorflow/python/keras/utils/losses_utils.py:170: to_float (from tensorflow.python.ops.math_ops) is deprecated and will be removed in a future version.
Instructions for updating:
Use tf.cast instead.

Fit the model¶

More the number of epochs, better will be the result. Notice how the loss keeps decreasing with each epoch.

In [5]:
model.fit(X,y, epochs = 3000, verbose=True)

WARNING:tensorflow:From /home/tanmay/anaconda3/lib/python3.7/site-packages/tensorflow/python/ops/math_ops.py:3066: to_int32 (from tensorflow.python.ops.math_ops) is deprecated and will be removed in a future version.
Instructions for updating:
Use tf.cast instead.

Test the model¶

Let's predict the price of a house having 7 bedrooms

In [6]:
model.predict([7])
Out[6]:
array([[400000.44]], dtype=float32)

The actual price¶

We can find the actual price, since we know what rule is used to calculate it.

Cost = 50k + (number_of_bedrooms * 50k)
In [7]:
50000 + (7 * 50000)
Out[7]:
400000

Conclusion¶

With just 6 datapoints, our model was able to make a pretty good guess. The actual price of the house with 7 bedrooms is so close to the predicted price. Fascinating, isn't it?
